FILE: config/host-scripts/check-system-ready

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#!/bin/bash
set -euo pipefail

# Load operational tunables from the data USB (placed here by load-scanner).
# shellcheck source=/dev/null
[ -f /var/lib/troskel/scanner.env ] && source /var/lib/troskel/scanner.env
CLAM_SIG_MAX_AGE_DAYS="${CLAM_SIG_MAX_AGE_DAYS:-30}"

PASS=0
FAIL=0

check() {
    local DESC="$1"
    local RESULT="$2"
    if [ "$RESULT" = "ok" ]; then
        printf "  [PASS] %s\n" "$DESC"
        PASS=$((PASS+1))
    else
        printf "  [FAIL] %s — %s\n" "$DESC" "$RESULT"
        FAIL=$((FAIL+1))
    fi
}

echo ""
echo "=== System readiness check ==="
echo ""

# Required external tools. The host scripts (load-scanner, scan-wrap,
# show-status, this script) depend on these being present in the CoreOS image.
# sha256sum in particular underwrites load-scanner's host-side rootfs
# verification: without it that verification cannot run. Checking the toolset
# here turns a silent assumption about the base image into a loud, diagnosable
# readiness failure, rather than an opaque "command not found" mid-load. If a
# future image drop ever removed coreutils, this is where it surfaces.
MISSING_TOOLS=""
for TOOL in sha256sum grep sed awk date head cp mkdir mount umount; do
    command -v "$TOOL" >/dev/null 2>&1 || MISSING_TOOLS="${MISSING_TOOLS} ${TOOL}"
done
check "Required tools present (sha256sum, coreutils, mount)" \
    "$([ -z "$MISSING_TOOLS" ] && echo ok || echo "missing:${MISSING_TOOLS}")"

NET=$(ip link show | grep -v "lo:" | grep -c "UP" || true)
check "No active network interfaces beyond loopback" \
    "$([ "$NET" -eq 0 ] && echo ok || echo "${NET} interface(s) active")"

check "KVM accessible" \
    "$([ -r /dev/kvm ] && [ -w /dev/kvm ] && echo ok || echo "not accessible")"

check "Scanner image loaded" \
    "$([ -f /var/lib/troskel/scanner-rootfs.ext4 ] && echo ok || echo "not found")"

check "Guest kernel loaded" \
    "$([ -f /var/lib/troskel/vmlinux ] && echo ok || echo "not found")"

ZINC=$(systemctl is-enabled zincati 2>/dev/null || echo "unknown")
check "Auto-update (zincati) is disabled" \
    "$([ "$ZINC" = "masked" ] && echo ok || echo "status: $ZINC")"

NET_IN_SCAN=$(grep -c "network-interfaces" /usr/local/bin/scan-wrap 2>/dev/null || true)
check "No network interface in scan config" \
    "$([ "$NET_IN_SCAN" -eq 0 ] && echo ok || echo "network config found — review scan-wrap")"

if [ -f /var/lib/troskel/signature-date ]; then
    SIG_DATE="$(cat /var/lib/troskel/signature-date)"
    SIG_EPOCH="$(date -d "$SIG_DATE" +%s 2>/dev/null || echo 0)"
    NOW_EPOCH="$(date +%s)"
    AGE_DAYS=$(( (NOW_EPOCH - SIG_EPOCH) / 86400 ))
    check "Signature date present and fresh (age: ${AGE_DAYS} days)" \
        "$([ "$AGE_DAYS" -le "$CLAM_SIG_MAX_AGE_DAYS" ] && echo ok || echo "signatures are ${AGE_DAYS} days old — run update")"
else
    check "Signature date present" "not found"
fi

echo ""
echo "=== Results: ${PASS} passed, ${FAIL} failed ==="
echo ""

if [ "$FAIL" -gt 0 ]; then
    echo "[!] One or more checks failed. Do not scan until resolved."
    echo "    Contact the admin if you are unsure how to proceed."
    exit 1
else
    echo "[+] All checks passed. System is ready to scan."
    exit 0
fi

FILE: config/host-scripts/load-scanner

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#!/bin/bash
set -euo pipefail
# DATA_USB and DEST default to the real device and load location. They are
# overridable from the environment only so tests/test-load-scanner.sh can
# drive the copy-and-verify logic against fixture directories without a real
# USB or root. Production leaves both unset, so the defaults apply.
DATA_USB="${DATA_USB:-/dev/disk/by-label/TROSKEL-DATA}"
DEST="${DEST:-/var/lib/troskel}"
# MOUNT may be pre-supplied (a populated fixture directory) so the verify
# logic can be tested without a real device or root; in that case we skip the
# mount and unmount and treat MOUNT as already populated. Production leaves it
# unset: we create a temp dir and mount the USB read-only onto it.
TEST_MOUNT="${MOUNT:-}"
MOUNT="${MOUNT:-$(mktemp -d)}"
echo "[*] Loading scanner from data USB..."
if [ -z "$TEST_MOUNT" ]; then
    mount -o ro "$DATA_USB" "$MOUNT" \
        || { echo "[!] Data USB not found. Is it plugged in?"; exit 1; }
fi

# Unmount on the way out, but only if we mounted (production). In test mode
# MOUNT is a caller-supplied fixture directory we must not touch.
cleanup_mount() {
    [ -z "$TEST_MOUNT" ] && umount "$MOUNT"
    return 0
}
mkdir -p "$DEST"
cp "$MOUNT/scanner-rootfs.ext4" "$DEST/"
cp "$MOUNT/vmlinux"             "$DEST/"
cp "$MOUNT/signature-date"      "$DEST/"
cp "$MOUNT/yara-rules-date"     "$DEST/"
cp "$MOUNT/scanner.env"         "$DEST/"

# scanner-rootfs.ext4 verification, host side.
#
# CONTRACT (consumer side): scanner-rootfs.ext4 is built and hashed by
# scripts/build-scanner-image.sh, written to TROSKEL-DATA with its sidecar
# scanner-rootfs.ext4.sha256 by scripts/prepare-data-usb.sh (which verifies
# the USB copy at write time via scripts/lib/verify-artefact.sh). This is the
# air-gap consumer: the rootfs copied here is the executable image the scanner
# VM runs, so it MUST be verified before it is trusted, and verification MUST
# re-read the copy under $DEST (the bytes that will execute), not the USB.
#
# This duplicates the verify-artefact.sh logic rather than sourcing it because
# that module is not yet shipped to the CoreOS host image (no plumbing exists
# to place it there; see the sign-data-usb-manifest / verify-artefact host
# story). verify-artefact.sh remains the canonical implementation; this inline
# check mirrors its two load-bearing safety properties and must be kept in step
# with it:
#   1. resolve the artefact under $DEST, never at a path the sidecar names;
#   2. reject any sidecar whose filename field is absolute or contains a slash
#      or is a traversal (the historical bug 2: a path-bearing sidecar made
#      verification follow the path back to the source instead of the copy).
#
# Absence of the sidecar is tolerated (an old USB predating sidecars), but a
# present-but-failing verification is FATAL: unlike the manifest (metadata, a
# warning), the rootfs is the executable image, so a corrupt or unverifiable
# rootfs must never be loaded. On failure the bad copy is removed and the
# script exits non-zero.
#
# NOTE: this verifies INTEGRITY only (bytes intact). It does not establish
# AUTHENTICITY (that the image came from this build station); a co-resident
# sidecar can be recomputed by anyone who can rewrite the medium. Authenticity
# is the sign-data-usb-manifest card, which adds a signature gate ahead of
# this check.
ROOTFS="$DEST/scanner-rootfs.ext4"
SIDECAR_SRC="$MOUNT/scanner-rootfs.ext4.sha256"
if [ -f "$SIDECAR_SRC" ]; then
    cp "$SIDECAR_SRC" "$DEST/"
    SIDECAR="$DEST/scanner-rootfs.ext4.sha256"
    LINE="$(head -n1 "$SIDECAR")"
    # Safe shape: 64 lowercase hex, two spaces, a filename with no slash.
    # This single check rejects empty/garbage lines, wrong hash length,
    # uppercase hex, and any absolute or directory-bearing path field.
    if ! printf '%s' "$LINE" | grep -qE '^[0-9a-f]{64}  [^/]+$'; then
        echo "[!] scanner-rootfs.ext4.sha256 is not in safe 'sha256sum <basename>' form:" >&2
        echo "      $LINE" >&2
        echo "    A path-bearing sidecar is rejected here; it would otherwise let" >&2
        echo "    verification check the wrong file. Refusing to load the scanner." >&2
        rm -f "$ROOTFS"
        cleanup_mount
        exit 1
    fi
    FILE_FIELD="$(printf '%s' "$LINE" | sed 's/^[0-9a-f]\{64\}  //')"
    if [ "$FILE_FIELD" = ".." ] || [ "$FILE_FIELD" = "." ]; then
        echo "[!] scanner-rootfs.ext4.sha256 filename field is a traversal: '$FILE_FIELD'" >&2
        echo "    Refusing to load the scanner." >&2
        rm -f "$ROOTFS"
        cleanup_mount
        exit 1
    fi
    EXPECTED="$(printf '%s' "$LINE" | awk '{print $1}')"
    # Re-read from $DEST: the copy that will be executed, not the USB.
    ACTUAL="$(sha256sum "$ROOTFS" | awk '{print $1}')"
    if [ "$ACTUAL" != "$EXPECTED" ]; then
        echo "[!] scanner-rootfs.ext4 failed verification on the host." >&2
        echo "    expected: $EXPECTED" >&2
        echo "    actual  : $ACTUAL" >&2
        echo "    The copied image does not match its sidecar. It may be corrupt or" >&2
        echo "    truncated. Refusing to load the scanner; removing the bad copy." >&2
        rm -f "$ROOTFS"
        cleanup_mount
        exit 1
    fi
    echo "[+] scanner-rootfs.ext4 verified against sidecar."
else
    echo "[!] No scanner-rootfs.ext4.sha256 on this data USB; cannot verify the"
    echo "    scanner image. This USB predates sidecar support. Rewrite it on the"
    echo "    build station to obtain a verifiable image. Loading unverified."
fi

# build-manifest.json propagation, USB -> /var/lib/troskel.
#
# CONTRACT (propagator/consumer side): the manifest is generated by
# scripts/generate-build-records.sh, written to this USB by
# scripts/prepare-data-usb.sh (which verifies it against the USB before the
# medium leaves the build station), and parsed by
# config/host-scripts/show-status for build identity. This script is the
# host-side hop: data USB -> /var/lib/troskel.
#
# Absence is tolerated here, unlike at write time: a data USB written before
# manifests existed legitimately has none, and the scanner must still load.
# Presence-but-corrupt is NOT silently tolerated: a manifest that copies but
# does not carry the fields show-status reads is reported, so the operator
# sees "manifest unreadable" rather than show-status quietly printing
# "unknown" as though the USB were simply old. The manifest is operational
# metadata, not a security gate (signed-manifest verification is future Tier
# 2 work), so a corrupt manifest is a visible warning, not a refusal to load
# the scanner: refusing to boot over bad metadata would be the wrong failure
# mode. No jq on the scanning host; we reuse the same grep-based field
# extraction show-status uses, so "usable here" means "usable there".
if [ -f "$MOUNT/build-manifest.json" ]; then
    cp "$MOUNT/build-manifest.json" "$DEST/"
    # Post-condition: re-read the destination copy and confirm the fields
    # show-status depends on actually extract. generated_at and troskel_commit
    # are quoted strings; troskel_dirty is an unquoted JSON boolean, so its
    # matcher differs (see show-status, which shares this shape).
    DEST_MAN="$DEST/build-manifest.json"
    man_field() {  # man_field <key>  -> quoted-string value, or empty
        grep -o "\"$1\"[[:space:]]*:[[:space:]]*\"[^\"]*\"" "$DEST_MAN" 2>/dev/null \
            | head -1 | sed 's/.*"\([^"]*\)"$/\1/'
    }
    MAN_GEN="$(man_field generated_at)"
    MAN_COMMIT="$(man_field troskel_commit)"
    # troskel_dirty: unquoted boolean, matched separately.
    MAN_DIRTY="$(grep -o "\"troskel_dirty\"[[:space:]]*:[[:space:]]*\(true\|false\)" "$DEST_MAN" 2>/dev/null \
        | head -1 | grep -o '\(true\|false\)$')"
    if [ -z "$MAN_GEN" ] || [ -z "$MAN_COMMIT" ] || [ -z "$MAN_DIRTY" ]; then
        echo "[!] build-manifest.json copied from the USB but is missing build-identity"
        echo "    fields (generated_at, troskel_commit, troskel_dirty). The manifest may"
        echo "    be corrupt or from an incompatible build. show-status will report the"
        echo "    affected fields as 'unreadable'. Scanner load continues; this is"
        echo "    metadata only, not a scan gate."
    fi
fi

cleanup_mount
echo "[+] Scanner loaded. Signature date: $(cat $DEST/signature-date)"

FILE: config/host-scripts/scan-wrap

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#!/bin/bash
# scan-wrap: host-side Firecracker wrapper
# Usage: scan-wrap <directory-to-scan>
#
# Phase 0 hardening (interim mitigation for docs/roadmap/ingest-vm.md):
#   - The previous `mkfs.ext4 -F -d "$TARGET_DIR"` walk reflected every
#     node type in the source tree (symlinks, device nodes, FIFOs,
#     sockets) into the constructed scanfiles image. The walk is now a
#     two-step process: first stage regular files and directories into a
#     fresh tree using `find -type f -o -type d`, then construct the
#     image from the staging tree.
#   - Hard caps on file count, tree depth, and total bytes are enforced
#     before image construction. Any cap breach aborts before mkfs runs.
#     Fail-closed; no partial image is presented to the scanner VM.
#   - The staging copy uses tar in pipe mode with --no-recursion on the
#     producer side and a paranoid set of options on the consumer side
#     (--no-overwrite-dir, default rejection of absolute paths). Neither
#     tar invocation dereferences symlinks: --warning=no-file-changed
#     makes a symlink that races into being between find's enumeration
#     and tar's open a silent drop rather than a followed link.
#   - A post-stage assertion confirms the staging tree contains only
#     regular files and directories before image construction begins.
#
# The caps live as constants in this script for Phase 0. The ingest-VM
# work (Phase 2) migrates them to scanner.env keys with engine-prefixed
# names matching the wider per-engine sizing convention.
set -euo pipefail

TARGET_DIR="${1:?Usage: scan-wrap <directory-to-scan>}"
SIGDIR="/var/lib/troskel"
BASE_IMAGE="${SIGDIR}/scanner-rootfs.ext4"
KERNEL="${SIGDIR}/vmlinux"
LOG_DIR="/var/log/troskel"
SCAN_LOG="${LOG_DIR}/scan-$(date -u +%Y%m%dT%H%M%SZ).log"
API_SOCKET="/tmp/troskel-$$.socket"
WORK="$(mktemp -d --tmpdir troskel-XXXXXX)"

# Load operational tunables. On the scanning host this file is placed at
# /var/lib/troskel/scanner.env by load-scanner from the data USB.
SCANNER_ENV="${SIGDIR}/scanner.env"
# shellcheck source=/dev/null
[ -f "$SCANNER_ENV" ] && source "$SCANNER_ENV"
# Defaults: match scanner.env defaults so scan-wrap works on a dev host
# where scanner.env may not be present (e.g. during make scan in CI).
GUEST_VCPU_COUNT="${GUEST_VCPU_COUNT:-2}"
GUEST_MEM_MIB="${GUEST_MEM_MIB:-2048}"
SCAN_IMG_SIZE="${SCAN_IMG_SIZE:-4G}"

# Phase 0 ingest caps. Hard-coded; migrated to scanner.env when the
# ingest VM lands.
#   STAGE_MAX_FILE_COUNT: count of regular files in the source tree.
#   STAGE_MAX_TREE_DEPTH: max directory depth, counted from the source
#                         root inclusive.
#   STAGE_MAX_TOTAL_BYTES: sum of regular-file sizes. Sits below
#                          SCAN_IMG_SIZE (4 GiB default) with margin for
#                          ext4 metadata overhead.
STAGE_MAX_FILE_COUNT=100000
STAGE_MAX_TREE_DEPTH=32
STAGE_MAX_TOTAL_BYTES=$((3750 * 1024 * 1024))   # 3.75 GiB

FC_PID=""

cleanup() {
    [ -n "$FC_PID" ] && kill "$FC_PID" 2>/dev/null || true
    rm -rf "$WORK"
    rm -f  "$API_SOCKET"
}
trap cleanup EXIT INT TERM

[ -f "$BASE_IMAGE" ] || { echo "[!] Scanner image not found. Was load-scanner successful?"; exit 1; }
[ -f "$KERNEL"     ] || { echo "[!] Kernel not found. Was load-scanner successful?"; exit 1; }
[ -r /dev/kvm ] && [ -w /dev/kvm ] \
    || { echo "[!] KVM not accessible. This machine may not support hardware virtualisation."; exit 1; }
[ -d "$TARGET_DIR" ] || { echo "[!] Directory not found: $TARGET_DIR"; exit 1; }

mkdir -p "$LOG_DIR"

EPHEMERAL="${WORK}/rootfs.ext4"
cp --sparse=always "$BASE_IMAGE" "$EPHEMERAL"

# ── Staged source-tree construction ───────────────────────────────────────────
# Build a clean staging tree containing only regular files and the
# directories needed to hold them. Symlinks, device nodes, FIFOs, and
# sockets are excluded by construction; the resulting ext4 image cannot
# contain them regardless of what was on the file USB.
#
# Caps are enforced before any copying begins. The `find -xdev` flag
# constrains the walk to a single filesystem so a stray bind mount or
# automounted submount cannot expand the workload past the cap.
STAGE_DIR="${WORK}/stage"
mkdir -p "$STAGE_DIR"

echo "[*] Enumerating source tree..."

# Tree-depth check. -mindepth N+1 catches any path strictly deeper than
# the cap. A single positive hit aborts; we do not need to enumerate all
# violators. -print -quit stops find on first match for low cost.
if find "$TARGET_DIR" -xdev -mindepth "$((STAGE_MAX_TREE_DEPTH + 1))" -print -quit 2>/dev/null | grep -q .; then
    echo "[!] Source tree exceeds maximum depth (${STAGE_MAX_TREE_DEPTH})."
    echo "    Reduce the directory nesting on the file USB and retry."
    exit 1
fi

# File-count check. Counting with find avoids loading the full file list
# into shell memory; the count itself is bounded by the cap check below.
FILE_COUNT="$(find "$TARGET_DIR" -xdev -type f 2>/dev/null | wc -l)"
if [ "$FILE_COUNT" -gt "$STAGE_MAX_FILE_COUNT" ]; then
    echo "[!] Source tree contains ${FILE_COUNT} files, exceeding the cap of ${STAGE_MAX_FILE_COUNT}."
    echo "    Reduce the number of files on the file USB and retry."
    exit 1
fi

# Total-bytes check. `find -printf '%s\n'` is GNU-specific but available
# on the CoreOS host; on a dev box without GNU find, stat is the fallback.
if find --version 2>/dev/null | grep -q GNU; then
    TOTAL_BYTES="$(find "$TARGET_DIR" -xdev -type f -printf '%s\n' 2>/dev/null \
        | awk '{s+=$1} END{print s+0}')"
else
    TOTAL_BYTES="$(find "$TARGET_DIR" -xdev -type f -exec stat -c '%s' {} + 2>/dev/null \
        | awk '{s+=$1} END{print s+0}')"
fi
if [ "$TOTAL_BYTES" -gt "$STAGE_MAX_TOTAL_BYTES" ]; then
    echo "[!] Source tree totals ${TOTAL_BYTES} bytes, exceeding the cap of ${STAGE_MAX_TOTAL_BYTES} bytes."
    echo "    Reduce the size of the transfer and retry."
    exit 1
fi

echo "[*] Staging ${FILE_COUNT} regular file(s), ${TOTAL_BYTES} bytes..."

# Stage via find piping into tar in store-and-extract mode. The first
# tar reads the null-delimited list and writes a tar stream to stdout
# without recursing into the listed entries; the second tar extracts the
# stream into the staging directory. The stream is restricted to regular
# files and directories by find's -type filter, so the staging tree
# physically cannot contain symlinks, device nodes, FIFOs, or sockets.
#
# Symlink-race defence. `find -type f` returns paths whose lstat at
# enumeration time was a regular file. An attacker with write access to
# the source tree could, in principle, race a symlink into being between
# the find call and the producer tar's open of each path. The
# countermeasures here:
#
#   - Neither tar invocation passes -h or --dereference. GNU tar without
#     these flags refuses to follow symlinks; if a path resolves to a
#     symlink at archive time, tar archives the symlink itself (not its
#     target). The find -type filter has already excluded symlinks from
#     the input list, so any symlink that appears at archive time is
#     necessarily a post-enumeration race.
#   - --warning=no-file-changed downgrades "file changed as we read it"
#     to a warning rather than aborting the whole archive; combined with
#     the find-time type filter, a raced symlink results in the file
#     being silently omitted from the staging tree, which is the
#     fail-closed outcome we want.
#   - --one-file-system on the producer prevents crossing a mount
#     surfaced after the find call.
#   - The consumer rejects absolute paths (default behaviour without
#     --absolute-names) and does not preserve ownership (--no-same-owner).
#     The staging tree is read by the host as root for image
#     construction; preserving owner from untrusted input is not useful.
#   - --no-overwrite-dir on the consumer prevents directory metadata in
#     the archive from overriding the staging root's own metadata.
#
# The net effect is that the staging tree contains only regular files
# and directories that survived a second lstat at archive time. Anything
# that became a symlink between find and tar is dropped, not followed.
#
# find's -L is not used: symlinks are not followed. tar in the producer
# stage uses --no-recursion so it does not re-expand directories that
# find already enumerated.
( cd "$TARGET_DIR" && \
  find . -xdev \( -type f -o -type d \) -print0 \
  | tar --null --no-recursion --one-file-system \
        --warning=no-file-changed \
        -cf - --files-from=- \
  | tar --no-same-owner --no-overwrite-dir \
        -xf - -C "$STAGE_DIR" ) \
  || { echo "[!] Failed to stage source tree."; exit 1; }

# Post-stage assertion. If any non-regular, non-directory entry made it
# through the pipeline, abort before image construction. This is a
# belt-and-braces check against a tar implementation surprise; the find
# and tar filters already exclude these types by construction.
if find "$STAGE_DIR" -xdev \! -type f \! -type d -print -quit 2>/dev/null | grep -q .; then
    echo "[!] Staging tree contains non-regular, non-directory entries."
    echo "    This should not be possible. Aborting before image construction."
    exit 1
fi

# ── Image construction ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# Build the scan image from the sanitised staging tree, not from the
# original mount. The previous `mkfs.ext4 -d "$TARGET_DIR"` call is gone.
SCAN_IMG="${WORK}/scanfiles.ext4"
truncate -s "${SCAN_IMG_SIZE}" "$SCAN_IMG"
mkfs.ext4 -F -d "$STAGE_DIR" "$SCAN_IMG" 2>/dev/null

cat > "${WORK}/fc-config.json" <<EOF
{
  "boot-source": {
    "kernel_image_path": "${KERNEL}",
    "boot_args": "console=ttyS0 reboot=k panic=1 root=/dev/vda rw quiet loglevel=0"
  },
  "drives": [
    {
      "drive_id":       "rootfs",
      "path_on_host":   "${EPHEMERAL}",
      "is_root_device": true,
      "is_read_only":   false
    },
    {
      "drive_id":       "scanfiles",
      "path_on_host":   "${SCAN_IMG}",
      "is_root_device": false,
      "is_read_only":   true
    }
  ],
  "machine-config": {
    "vcpu_count":   ${GUEST_VCPU_COUNT},
    "mem_size_mib": ${GUEST_MEM_MIB},
    "smt":          false
  }
}
EOF

echo "[*] Starting scan. This may take several minutes..."
echo "[*] Log: $SCAN_LOG"
echo ""

: > "${WORK}/fc-hypervisor.log"   # Firecracker won't create it itself

firecracker \
    --api-sock    "$API_SOCKET" \
    --config-file "${WORK}/fc-config.json" \
    --log-path    "${WORK}/fc-hypervisor.log" \
    --level       Warn \
    > >(tee -a "$SCAN_LOG") 2>&1 &
FC_PID=$!

wait "$FC_PID" || true
FC_PID=""

# Per-engine summary. Extract the ENGINE: lines emitted by the
# guest entrypoint and reformat them for the operator. The
# values are read from a controlled grammar (status= one of
# clean/threat/error, count= a non-negative integer); we
# validate both before display so a malformed or hostile log
# cannot inject formatting onto the operator's terminal.
summarise_engine() {
    local NAME="$1"          # display label, e.g. "ClamAV"
    local TAG="$2"           # ENGINE tag in the log, e.g. "clamav"
    local LINE STATUS COUNT
    LINE="$(grep "^\[..:..:..\] ENGINE: ${TAG} " "$SCAN_LOG" | tail -1 || true)"
    if [ -z "$LINE" ]; then
        printf "  %-8s : no result\n" "$NAME"
        return
    fi
    STATUS="$(echo "$LINE" | sed -n 's/.* status=\([a-z]*\) .*/\1/p')"
    COUNT="$( echo "$LINE" | sed -n 's/.* count=\([0-9]*\).*/\1/p')"
    case "$STATUS" in
        clean)  printf "  %-8s : clean\n" "$NAME" ;;
        threat) printf "  %-8s : THREAT (%s flagged)\n" "$NAME" "${COUNT:-?}" ;;
        error)  printf "  %-8s : ERROR\n" "$NAME" ;;
        *)      printf "  %-8s : unknown\n" "$NAME" ;;
    esac
}

# show_findings: display flagged items from the scan log in a readable
# format for the operator. Extracts ClamAV FOUND lines and LOKI-RS ALERT
# records, strips internal paths, and truncates at MAX_FINDINGS items.
show_findings() {
    local LOG="$1"
    local MAX_FINDINGS=20
    local COUNT=0

    # ClamAV: "path: SignatureName FOUND"
    # Strip /mnt/scanfiles/ prefix so the operator sees the path relative
    # to what was on the file USB, not the internal mount path.
    local CLAM_FINDINGS
    CLAM_FINDINGS="$(grep ' FOUND$' "$LOG" 2>/dev/null \
        | sed 's|/mnt/scanfiles/||; s|: | — |' \
        || true)"

    if [ -n "$CLAM_FINDINGS" ]; then
        echo ""
        echo "  Flagged by ClamAV:"
        while IFS= read -r LINE; do
            [ -z "$LINE" ] && continue
            printf "    %s\n" "$LINE"
            COUNT=$((COUNT + 1))
            [ "$COUNT" -ge "$MAX_FINDINGS" ] && { echo "    ... (see full log for more)"; break; }
        done <<< "$CLAM_FINDINGS"
    fi

    # LOKI-RS: JSONL lines with "level":"ALERT"
    # Extract file and rule fields. Use python3 if available; fall back to
    # a grep+sed heuristic that handles the common case.
    local LOKI_FINDINGS
    LOKI_FINDINGS="$(grep '"level":"ALERT"' "$LOG" 2>/dev/null || true)"

    if [ -n "$LOKI_FINDINGS" ]; then
        echo ""
        echo "  Flagged by LOKI-RS:"
        COUNT=0
        if command -v python3 >/dev/null 2>&1; then
            echo "$LOKI_FINDINGS" | python3 -c '
import sys, json
for line in sys.stdin:
    line = line.strip()
    if not line: continue
    try:
        j = json.loads(line)
        f = j.get("file", "?").replace("/mnt/scanfiles/", "")
        r = j.get("rule", "?")
        print(f"    {f} --- {r}")
    except Exception:
        print(f"    {line[:120]}")
' 2>/dev/null | head -"$MAX_FINDINGS" || true
        else
            echo "$LOKI_FINDINGS" \
                | sed 's/.*"file":"\([^"]*\)".*/\1/' \
                | sed 's|/mnt/scanfiles/||' \
                | head -"$MAX_FINDINGS" \
                | sed 's/^/    /' \
                || true
        fi
    fi
}

echo ""
if grep -q "VERDICT: THREAT DETECTED" "$SCAN_LOG"; then
    printf '\033[1;41m                                                \033[0m\n'
    printf '\033[1;41m   *** THREAT DETECTED — DO NOT TRANSFER ***    \033[0m\n'
    printf '\033[1;41m                                                \033[0m\n'
    echo ""
    summarise_engine "ClamAV"  "clamav"
    summarise_engine "LOKI-RS" "loki"
    show_findings "$SCAN_LOG"
    echo ""
    echo "  Do not transfer any files from this USB."
    echo "  Full log: $SCAN_LOG"
    echo "  (Photograph this screen before powering off — the log is lost on shutdown)"
elif grep -q "VERDICT: CLEAN" "$SCAN_LOG"; then
    printf '\033[1;42m                                                \033[0m\n'
    printf '\033[1;42m   *** CLEAN — Files may proceed               \033[0m\n'
    printf '\033[1;42m                                                \033[0m\n'
    echo ""
    summarise_engine "ClamAV"  "clamav"
    summarise_engine "LOKI-RS" "loki"
    echo ""
    echo "  Full log: $SCAN_LOG"
else
    printf '\033[1;43m                                                \033[0m\n'
    printf '\033[1;43m   *** RESULT UNCLEAR — Contact admin           \033[0m\n'
    printf '\033[1;43m                                                \033[0m\n'
    echo ""
    summarise_engine "ClamAV"  "clamav"
    summarise_engine "LOKI-RS" "loki"
    echo ""
    echo "  The scanner did not complete normally."
    echo "  The files have NOT been scanned. Do not transfer them."
    echo ""
    echo "  Contact the admin with this information:"
    echo "    Log: $SCAN_LOG"
    echo "    (Photograph this screen before powering off — the log is lost on shutdown)"
fi

================================================================================

FILE: config/host-scripts/show-status

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#!/bin/bash
echo ""
echo "=== Scanner status ==="
SIG="$(cat /var/lib/troskel/signature-date 2>/dev/null || echo 'not loaded')"
YARA="$(cat /var/lib/troskel/yara-rules-date 2>/dev/null || echo 'not loaded')"
echo "  Signature date : $SIG"
echo "  YARA rules date: $YARA"
if [ -f /var/lib/troskel/scanner-rootfs.ext4 ]; then
    SZ="$(du -sh /var/lib/troskel/scanner-rootfs.ext4 | cut -f1)"
    echo "  Scanner image  : loaded ($SZ)"
else
    echo "  Scanner image  : NOT LOADED"
fi
if [ -r /dev/kvm ] && [ -w /dev/kvm ]; then
    echo "  KVM            : available"
else
    echo "  KVM            : NOT AVAILABLE — scanning will fail"
fi
LAST="$(ls -t /var/log/troskel/ 2>/dev/null | head -1)"
if [ -n "$LAST" ]; then
    RESULT="$(grep 'VERDICT' /var/log/troskel/"$LAST" 2>/dev/null | tail -1 || echo 'unknown')"
    echo "  Last scan      : $LAST"
    echo "  Last result    : $RESULT"
else
    echo "  Last scan      : none this session"
fi

# Build identity from the per-build manifest.
#
# CONTRACT (consumer side): the manifest is generated by
# scripts/generate-build-records.sh, written to the data USB by
# scripts/prepare-data-usb.sh (which verifies it against the USB at write
# time), and copied to /var/lib/troskel by config/host-scripts/load-scanner.
# This block is the final consumer.
#
# Three states, distinguished deliberately:
#   - absent: an old data USB written before manifests existed. Report
#     "unknown" and say so plainly. Not an error.
#   - present and parseable: report the fields.
#   - present but missing required fields: corrupt or drifted manifest.
#     Report "unreadable" rather than "unknown", so the operator can tell a
#     corrupt manifest from a genuinely old USB. load-scanner already warns at
#     load time; this is the matching display state.
#
# Parsing without jq (not installed on the scanning host); fields are stable,
# grep+sed suffices. Note the two value shapes: generated_at and
# troskel_commit are quoted strings; troskel_dirty is an UNQUOTED JSON boolean
# (generate-build-records.sh emits `"troskel_dirty": false`, no quotes), so it
# needs its own matcher. An earlier version of this block used the quoted-
# string matcher for troskel_dirty, which never matched, so "Tree clean"
# always printed "unknown". If generate-build-records.sh changes how it emits
# this field, update the matcher here and the verification in
# prepare-data-usb.sh / load-scanner together.
# MANIFEST defaults to the loaded location; overridable only so the
# regression test (tests/test-manifest-propagation.sh) can point the parser
# at fixture files without a real /var/lib/troskel. Production has it unset,
# so the default applies.
MANIFEST="${MANIFEST:-/var/lib/troskel/build-manifest.json}"
echo ""
echo "=== Scanner build ==="
if [ -f "$MANIFEST" ]; then
    extract_str() {
        # extract_str <key>  reads "<key>": "<value>" (quoted string) from $MANIFEST.
        grep -o "\"$1\"[[:space:]]*:[[:space:]]*\"[^\"]*\"" "$MANIFEST" 2>/dev/null \
            | head -1 \
            | sed 's/.*"\([^"]*\)"$/\1/'
    }
    GEN="$(extract_str generated_at)"
    COMMIT="$(extract_str troskel_commit)"
    # troskel_dirty is an unquoted boolean; match true/false, not a string.
    DIRTY="$(grep -o "\"troskel_dirty\"[[:space:]]*:[[:space:]]*\(true\|false\)" "$MANIFEST" 2>/dev/null \
        | head -1 | grep -o '\(true\|false\)$')"

    if [ -z "$GEN" ] && [ -z "$COMMIT" ] && [ -z "$DIRTY" ]; then
        # File exists but none of the expected fields extract: corrupt or
        # structurally drifted. Distinct from the absent case below.
        echo "  Generated      : unreadable"
        echo "  Troskel commit : unreadable"
        echo "  Tree clean     : unreadable"
        echo "  (build manifest present but could not be parsed — it may be"
        echo "   corrupt or from an incompatible build; load-scanner warned at"
        echo "   load time)"
    else
        echo "  Generated      : ${GEN:-unknown}"
        echo "  Troskel commit : ${COMMIT:-unknown}"
        if [ "$DIRTY" = "false" ]; then
            echo "  Tree clean     : yes"
        elif [ "$DIRTY" = "true" ]; then
            echo "  Tree clean     : NO — uncommitted changes at build time"
        else
            echo "  Tree clean     : unknown"
        fi
    fi
else
    # No manifest on the data USB. Per the contract above, this means an old
    # USB predating manifest support: write-time generation is now mandatory,
    # so a freshly written USB always carries one.
    echo "  Generated      : unknown"
    echo "  Troskel commit : unknown"
    echo "  Tree clean     : unknown"
    echo "  (no build manifest on this data USB — it predates manifest support;"
    echo "   rewrite it on the build station to populate build identity)"
fi
echo ""

================================================================================

FILE: config/host-scripts/troskel

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#!/bin/bash
# troskel: operator entry point.
#
# Phase 0 hardening (interim mitigation for docs/roadmap/ingest-vm.md):
#   - Filesystem type is determined by blkid on the host and constrained
#     to a fixed allowlist (ext4, vfat). Unsupported filesystems are
#     refused before any mount is attempted.
#   - The mount call passes -t <fs> explicitly, eliminating the host
#     kernel's filesystem autodetection path.
#   - The mount uses -o ro,nodev,nosuid,noexec.
#   - The mount is performed inside a private mount namespace (unshare
#     -m --propagation private) so the file USB is invisible to the
#     rest of the host and torn down with the namespace if the script
#     dies mid scan. The scan-wrap invocation runs inside the same
#     namespace.
#   - After mount, the script refuses to proceed if anything under the
#     mount root is itself a mountpoint (defence against a malicious
#     filesystem image carrying nested mount sources).
#
# The hotplug auto-selection (tail -1) is preserved in this phase. The
# explicit-selection rewrite lands with the ingest-VM work (Phase 2),
# where it composes with the new enumeration flow rather than being
# bolted onto the existing flow now.
set -euo pipefail

# Hard-coded allowlist. Mirrors the set documented in
# docs/OPERATOR-GUIDE.md. NTFS and exFAT are deliberately excluded; their
# kernel parsers carry more surface than the project is willing to expose
# even under the interim mitigation. Phase 2 moves filesystem detection
# behind the ingest VM but does not widen this set.
ALLOWED_FS=(ext4 vfat)

# Re-exec into a private mount namespace if we are not already in one.
# The TROSKEL_NS_ACTIVE sentinel prevents an unbounded re-exec loop.
# --propagation private detaches the namespace's mounts from the host's
# propagation tree so the file USB mount cannot leak back out, and the
# namespace's mounts are torn down automatically when the script exits.
if [ -z "${TROSKEL_NS_ACTIVE:-}" ]; then
    export TROSKEL_NS_ACTIVE=1
    exec unshare --mount --propagation private -- "$0" "$@"
fi

SCAN_DEV="${1:-}"
if [ -z "$SCAN_DEV" ]; then
    SCAN_DEV="$(lsblk -dpno NAME,HOTPLUG | awk '$2==1{print $1}' | tail -1)"
    [ -n "$SCAN_DEV" ] \
        || { echo "[!] No USB detected. Insert file USB and try again."; exit 1; }
    echo "[*] Detected file USB: $SCAN_DEV"
fi

# Determine filesystem type without mounting. blkid reads the superblock
# signature region only. The call is wrapped in a strict timeout and its
# output validated against the allowlist before being used. The -s TYPE
# -o value form returns a single bare token; anything else aborts.
FS_TYPE="$(timeout 5s blkid -s TYPE -o value "$SCAN_DEV" 2>/dev/null || true)"
if [ -z "$FS_TYPE" ]; then
    echo "[!] Could not determine filesystem type on $SCAN_DEV."
    echo "    The USB may be unformatted, encrypted, or its filesystem is"
    echo "    not recognised by blkid. Reformat as ext4 or FAT32 and retry."
    exit 1
fi

# Validate against the allowlist. Substring matching is avoided here: the
# value must match a list entry exactly. A blkid output of `ext4 ` with
# trailing whitespace, or `EXT4`, would fail this check by design.
FS_OK=0
for ALLOWED in "${ALLOWED_FS[@]}"; do
    if [ "$FS_TYPE" = "$ALLOWED" ]; then
        FS_OK=1
        break
    fi
done

if [ "$FS_OK" -ne 1 ]; then
    echo "[!] Filesystem '$FS_TYPE' on $SCAN_DEV is not supported."
    echo "    Supported filesystems: ${ALLOWED_FS[*]}"
    echo ""
    echo "    NTFS and exFAT are not supported as of this release. Reformat"
    echo "    the file USB as ext4 (Linux) or FAT32 (universal interchange)"
    echo "    and copy the files across, or use a different medium."
    exit 1
fi

mkdir -p /mnt/usb

# Mount with explicit -t. The kernel's filesystem-detection path is no
# longer reached. -o ro,nodev,nosuid,noexec is conservative against a
# malicious filesystem that attempts to present device nodes, set-uid
# binaries, or executable payloads at mount time; the post-mount tree
# walk in scan-wrap also excludes these node types by construction.
mount -t "$FS_TYPE" -o ro,nodev,nosuid,noexec "$SCAN_DEV" /mnt/usb \
    || { echo "[!] Failed to mount $SCAN_DEV as $FS_TYPE."; exit 1; }

echo "[+] File USB mounted read-only (filesystem: $FS_TYPE)."

# Nested-mountpoint refusal. A malicious filesystem image cannot create
# kernel mountpoints by itself, but bind mounts or automounter activity
# pre-existing on the host could surface under /mnt/usb. findmnt -R lists
# the mountpoint and any submounts; more than one line means submounts
# are present. Refuse rather than risk scanning content from a different
# filesystem than the one we just validated.
if [ "$(findmnt -Rno TARGET /mnt/usb 2>/dev/null | wc -l)" -gt 1 ]; then
    echo "[!] Nested mountpoints detected under /mnt/usb."
    echo "    The file USB or the host has surfaced a submount that"
    echo "    bypasses the filesystem allowlist. Refusing to scan."
    umount /mnt/usb 2>/dev/null || true
    exit 1
fi

/usr/local/bin/scan-wrap /mnt/usb
umount /mnt/usb 2>/dev/null || true
echo "[+] File USB unmounted."

================================================================================

FILE: config/scanner.env

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

# config/scanner.env
#
# Operational tunables for the scanner. Sourced by build-station scripts
# and propagated to the scanning host via the data USB (see below).
# Admins may adjust these values; changes take effect on the next
# troskel-build.sh run.
#
# Format: shell-sourceable KEY=VALUE. Same constraints as versions.env.
#
# Propagation:
#   - prepare-data-usb.sh copies this file to the data USB.
#   - load-scanner copies it from the USB to /var/lib/troskel/scanner.env.
#   - check-system-ready sources /var/lib/troskel/scanner.env at runtime.
#   Values used only at build time (VM sizing, scan image size, file caps)
#   never need to reach the scanning host.

# --- Freshness gates ----------------------------------------------------------
# Maximum age in days before check-system-ready fails the readiness check.
# Both thresholds must be satisfied for the system to be considered ready.
# An admin who sets either value to 0 or very large weakens the guarantee
# deliberately, this is recorded in SECURITY.md.

# ClamAV signatures update several times daily; 30 days is conservative.
CLAM_SIG_MAX_AGE_DAYS=30

# YARA Forge Core rules update less continuously than ClamAV signatures.
# 60 days is a reasonable default; tighten for higher-threat environments.
LOKI_YARA_MAX_AGE_DAYS=60

# --- Guest VM sizing ----------------------------------------------------------
# Firecracker microVM resources for the single-VM sequential scan.
# If parallel-engines lands, these become per-engine values (see that
# roadmap doc for the naming convention that will replace these).
GUEST_VCPU_COUNT=2
GUEST_MEM_MIB=2048

# --- Scan target --------------------------------------------------------------
# Size of the ext4 image materialised from the file USB for presentation
# to the guest as a read-only block device. Must be large enough to hold
# the largest anticipated transfer batch plus filesystem overhead (~10%).
SCAN_IMG_SIZE=4G

# --- Per-engine file size caps ------------------------------------------------
# Both engines silently skip files above their defaults, a false-negative
# vector for a transfer scanner. Both values below are set explicitly so the
# operator-relevant behaviour ("nothing on the USB is silently bypassed") is
# under deliberate control rather than relying on whatever the upstream
# defaults happen to be at the pinned version.

# LOKI-RS: maximum file size in bytes passed to --max-file-size.
# The upstream default is 64 MiB.
# WARNING: 0 does NOT mean unlimited in LOKI-RS; it means skip everything.
# Always set a concrete value.
LOKI_MAX_FILE_SIZE=4294967296

# ClamAV: maximum size in bytes passed to BOTH --max-filesize (per-file cap)
# and --max-scansize (cumulative cap on data extracted from within one
# archive). The upstream defaults are 100 MiB and 400 MiB respectively;
# both can silently skip content on a transfer scanner. We set both to the
# same value so the per-file and per-archive policies stay coupled.
CLAM_MAX_FILE_SIZE=4294967296

variant: fcos
version: 1.5.0

passwd:
  users:
    - name: scanner
      groups: [kvm, wheel]
      # The hash below is a sentinel. prepare-boot-usb.sh generates a
      # fresh passphrase at build time, hashes it with openssl passwd -6,
      # and substitutes the hash into a temp copy of this file before
      # invoking butane. Do not edit by hand, the committed value is
      # not a usable hash.
      password_hash: "@@SCANNER_PASSWORD_HASH@@"

storage:
  files:

    - path: /usr/local/bin/load-scanner
      mode: 0755
      contents:
        local: host-scripts/load-scanner

    - path: /usr/local/bin/scan-wrap
      mode: 0755
      contents:
        local: host-scripts/scan-wrap

    - path: /usr/local/bin/troskel
      mode: 0755
      contents:
        local: host-scripts/troskel

    - path: /usr/local/bin/show-status
      mode: 0755
      contents:
        local: host-scripts/show-status

    - path: /usr/local/bin/check-system-ready
      mode: 0755
      contents:
        local: host-scripts/check-system-ready

systemd:
  units:
    - name: load-scanner.service
      enabled: true
      contents: |
        [Unit]
        Description=Load scanner image from data USB into RAM
        After=local-fs.target
        Before=getty@tty1.service
        [Service]
        Type=oneshot
        ExecStart=/usr/local/bin/load-scanner
        RemainAfterExit=yes
        StandardOutput=journal+console
        [Install]
        WantedBy=multi-user.target

    - name: zincati.service
      mask: true

FILE: config/versions.env

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

# config/versions.env
#
# Central source of truth for upstream component versions. Sourced by the
# project's scripts. Bump deliberately; record the reason in the commit
# message, and update the SBOM.json register.
#
# Format: shell-sourceable KEY=VALUE. Keep it that way. The scripts use
# `source config/versions.env` rather than parsing this file. Don't put
# anything here that bash can't evaluate as a plain assignment.
#
# The project distinguishes two kinds of upstream input, treated differently:
#
#   SOFTWARE        Components that define how the scanner works (Firecracker,
#                   Butane, LOKI-RS, the kernel, the wordlist, etc). These
#                   are pinned to specific versions with recorded SHA-256
#                   constants. The verification question is "did we get the
#                   version we asked for". Bumping requires deliberate
#                   developer review and a new recorded hash.
#
#   DETECTION       Inputs that define what the scanner looks for (ClamAV
#                   signatures, YARA Forge rules, signature-base IOCs).
#                   These float by design. Fresh detection is the point.
#                   The verification question is operational: "what exactly
#                   was in use when a given scan ran, and can it be
#                   reproduced". Detection inputs are pinned to release
#                   tags where the upstream provides them (the LOKI IOC
#                   base), and integrity-verified at download where the
#                   upstream publishes sidecars or signatures (ClamAV via
#                   freshclam's embedded keys; Butane via GPG-bootstrap).
#                   Where the upstream publishes nothing (YARA Forge), the
#                   downloaded hash is logged at build time in the per-build
#                   manifest.
#
# Three categories of pinning are used:
#
#   PINNED          A specific version. Software components default here.
#                   Changes only with deliberate review.
#   PINNED-TAG      A specific release tag for a detection input that
#                   publishes tags. Bumped on each detection refresh; the
#                   resolved tag is recorded per build for reproducibility.
#   FLOATING        Tracks an upstream "latest" or moving channel. Used
#                   only where pinning is genuinely impractical; the
#                   resolved value at build time is recorded per build.
#   DERIVED         Not pinned here because it must match another pin
#                   (e.g. the guest kernel must match Firecracker's CI version).
#
# Variable naming: variables are named for the role they play in the build,
# not for the upstream identity. The LOKI_IOC_BASE_VERSION pins the IOC
# inputs used by LOKI-RS; the comment records which upstream repository
# supplies them. This means a reader who doesn't know the upstream still
# understands what each pin controls.
#
# SHA-256 verification: SOFTWARE components carry a *_SHA256 constant
# alongside the version. The download step verifies the fetched artefact
# against this value before installing. Bumping a version requires
# recording the new SHA-256 from the upstream sidecar (or, for Butane,
# from a one-time GPG-verified download); verification will fail visibly
# if the recorded and downloaded values go out of sync.

# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# PROJECT VERSION
# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Troskel product version. Single source of truth for the version string
# emitted into SBOM.json (component, purl, dependency ref, composition
# assembly) and consumed by the Makefile for image labelling. Bump
# deliberately on release; the tag (e.g. v1.0.0) must match.
#
# CONTRACT (producer side): this variable is read by
# scripts/generate-build-records.sh (SBOM product-version fields), by the
# Makefile (image build), and asserted against committed SBOM.json by
# tests/test-validate.sh. A bump here that is not followed by an SBOM
# regenerate on the build station is caught by that Tier 1 check.
TROSKEL_VERSION="1.0.0"

# Version of the build-records generator tool itself (the program that
# writes SBOM.json and build-manifest.json), recorded in the SBOM tools
# block. Versions independently of TROSKEL_VERSION: the product and the
# tool that describes it are not the same artefact and need not move
# together. They are coincidentally equal at 1.0.0.
TROSKEL_BUILD_RECORDS_GENERATOR_VERSION="1.0.0"

# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# SOFTWARE COMPONENTS
# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Firecracker microVM hypervisor (PINNED).
# The guest kernel must match the CI series for this version (see DERIVED below).
FC_VERSION="v1.7.0"
# SHA-256 of firecracker-${FC_VERSION}-x86_64.tgz from the GitHub release.
# Source: https://github.com/firecracker-microvm/firecracker/releases/download/v1.7.0/firecracker-v1.7.0-x86_64.tgz.sha256.txt
FC_SHA256="55bd3e6d599fdd108e36e52f9aee2319f06c18a90f2fa49b64e93fdf06f5ff53"

# LOKI-RS YARA/IOC scanner (PINNED).
# Bumping requires re-testing the guest entrypoint against any flag changes,
# AND verifying glibc compatibility with the guest rootfs (DEBIAN_RELEASE below).
LOKI_VERSION="v2.10.0"
# SHA-256 of loki-linux-x86_64-${LOKI_VERSION}.tar.gz from the GitHub release.
# Source: https://github.com/Neo23x0/Loki-RS/releases/download/v2.10.0/loki-linux-x86_64-v2.10.0.tar.gz.sha256
LOKI_SHA256="71ff1643736a05adbb37520fc05fdb9710ef4f972dad68d67caf2b98ac69dade"

# Butane (PINNED, was previously FLOATING).
# Butane compiles Ignition configs; its output format is stable.
# Pinned at the first checksum-verification pass; bump deliberately.
BUTANE_VERSION="v0.27.0"
# SHA-256 of butane-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu, recorded after one-time
# GPG verification of the upstream .asc signature. Butane does not
# publish SHA-256 sidecars; the .asc signature against the Fedora
# signing key is the upstream's integrity path. To bump:
#   1. Import the Fedora signing key:
#      curl -fsSL https://fedoraproject.org/fedora.gpg | gpg --import
#   2. Download the binary and .asc from the new release:
#      curl -fsSL -O https://github.com/coreos/butane/releases/download/<VERSION>/butane-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu
#      curl -fsSL -O https://github.com/coreos/butane/releases/download/<VERSION>/butane-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu.asc
#   3. gpg --verify butane-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu.asc butane-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu
#      Confirm "Good signature" (the "key not certified" warning is expected
#      - see docs/SECURITY.md for the trust model).
#   4. sha256sum the verified binary and record the value here.
BUTANE_SHA256="4691b2618e94e67bb5ad2d8954bb2a414f670b83e8a39b76faae42f3c1a879fe"

# EFF Long Wordlist used for diceware passphrase generation (PINNED).
# Pinned to a specific 2016 publication; the wordlist is stable upstream
# but the principle is to pin software components even when the upstream
# is stable in practice. Bumping requires recording a new hash.
# Source: https://www.eff.org/files/2016/07/18/eff_large_wordlist.txt
# Licence: CC-BY 3.0 — see THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES.md.
WORDLIST_URL="https://www.eff.org/files/2016/07/18/eff_large_wordlist.txt"
WORDLIST_SHA256="addd35536511597a02fa0a9ff1e5284677b8883b83e986e43f15a3db996b903e"

# coreos-installer container image (FLOATING: tracks the 'release' tag).
# Used only by prepare-boot-usb.sh to build the boot ISO.
# Pinning by digest is tracked as a planned future hardening step: it
# requires a different mechanism (docker pull by sha256 digest rather
# than SHA-256 of a downloaded file).
COREOS_INSTALLER_TAG="release"

# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# GUEST ROOTFS
# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Debian release used for the scanner guest rootfs (PINNED).
DEBIAN_RELEASE="trixie"

# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# SCANNING HOST
# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# CoreOS release stream (FLOATING — tracks the 'stable' channel).
# Used by prepare-boot-usb.sh. The CoreOS ISO is signed and verified by
# the Fedora signing key embedded in coreos-installer at extract time, so
# this artefact is verified upstream and does not need a SHA-256 here.
#
# By the project's "software components should be pinned" principle this
# should eventually be pinned to a specific CoreOS version. Tracked as a
# planned future hardening step because the bump cadence (CoreOS publishes
# security updates frequently) makes deliberate pinning a separate workflow
# change rather than a one-time pin. See SECURITY.md residual risks.
COREOS_STREAM="stable"

# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# DETECTION INPUTS
# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# LOKI-RS IOC base (PINNED-TAG).
# Pins the IOC inputs used by LOKI-RS: hash-iocs.txt, filename-iocs.txt,
# c2-iocs.txt. Supplied upstream by github.com/Neo23x0/signature-base.
# Pinned to a release tag rather than fetched from master so the build
# is reproducible: a scan that goes red can be re-run against the same
# IOC set later to confirm the verdict. Bump on each detection refresh.
# Source: https://github.com/Neo23x0/signature-base/releases
LOKI_IOC_BASE_VERSION="v2.0"

# YARA Forge rules and ClamAV signatures: not pinned here. Both float
# by design and have different integrity paths:
#
#   - ClamAV: freshclam verifies .cvd files against keys embedded in the
#     ClamAV binary at download time. Upstream-signed; no separate work
#     needed here.
#
#   - YARA Forge: publishes weekly releases of YARA rule archives, but
#     does NOT publish .sha256 sidecars or GPG signatures alongside its
#     release assets. TLS-from-GitHub is the only integrity guarantee
#     available at download time. The downloaded archive's SHA-256 is
#     logged at build time in the per-build manifest (generated by
#     scripts/generate-build-records.sh, propagated to the scanning host
#     and surfaced by show-status) so that a scan can be reproduced
#     later against a byte-exact rule set, even though there is no
#     upstream value to verify against.

# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# DERIVED (NOT PINNED HERE)
# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Guest kernel: derived from FC_VERSION. download-kernel.sh constructs the CI
# series (e.g. v1.7) from FC_VERSION; within that series, the specific patch
# version is recorded at first download (record-at-first-download pattern).
# Firecracker and its CI kernel are tightly coupled — a CI-series mismatch
# produces a guest that cannot see its drives — so the series itself stays
# derived from FC_VERSION. The patch version within the series is pinned
# below once recorded.
#
# The Firecracker CI S3 bucket does not publish per-asset SHA-256 sidecars,
# so the guest kernel uses a record-at-first-download pattern covering two
# values:
#
#   KERNEL_RESOLVED  The resolved kernel filename within the CI series
#                    (e.g. vmlinux-6.1.141).
#   KERNEL_SHA256    The SHA-256 of that kernel file.
#
# Both empty: next download will resolve 'latest' under the CI series,
# record both values, and write them back here. Both populated: next
# download will construct the URL from KERNEL_RESOLVED and verify the
# downloaded bytes against KERNEL_SHA256. Inconsistent state (one empty,
# the other populated) is rejected as a logic bug.
#
# To intentionally bump to a newer kernel, blank both values and re-run
# the build; the discover-and-record path will pick up the current
# 'latest' in the CI series. Do not edit the recorded values by hand —
# they should always be the output of a verified download.
KERNEL_RESOLVED="vmlinux-6.1.77"
KERNEL_SHA256="c29a3b3f1f99aea2a63cd5f73acf7036d493666c453324ed12621bf5d7bf7176"

FILE: CONTRIBUTING.md

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

# Contributing

This document covers project-process conventions: how to branch, commit, and tag. For build and test mechanics (Docker, make targets, the containerised pipeline), see [`docs/DEVELOPER.md`](docs/DEVELOPER.md).

## Git workflow

### Branches

`main` is the only long-lived branch. Work on anything non-trivial in a short-lived feature branch, then merge back via a pull request, even if you are the sole reviewer. This keeps the history readable and gives you a natural review checkpoint before code lands.

```bash
git checkout -b feat/parallel-engines
# do the work
git checkout main
git merge --no-ff feat/parallel-engines -m "feat: add parallel engine VM architecture"
git branch -d feat/parallel-engines
```

The `--no-ff` flag preserves a merge commit so the history shows that a body of related work landed together, rather than a flat stream of individual commits.

### Commit messages

Use a short type prefix. The full conventional commits spec is not enforced, but keeping the type consistent makes the log scannable.

```
feat: add capa as a third scan engine
fix: pass ext4 image directly to Firecracker, remove losetup
docs: update README admin workflow for troskel-build.sh
chore: rename SCANNER-DATA label to TROSKEL-DATA
refactor: extract guest scripts from build-scanner-image.sh heredocs
test: add POSIX sh compliance check to test-validate.sh
```

Useful types: `feat`, `fix`, `docs`, `chore`, `refactor`, `test`. Nothing else needed.

The subject line should complete the sentence "this commit will...". Keep it under 72 characters. If more context is needed, leave a blank line after the subject and write a body.

### Tags

Tag meaningful milestones, not every merge, but points worth being able to return to.

```bash
git tag -a v0.2.0 -m "feat: parallel engine VM architecture"
git push origin v0.2.0
```

A tag is a checkpoint, not a formal release; it does not need release notes at this stage.

### Before committing

Run `make validate` first. It catches Butane config errors, shellcheck failures, and guest script bashisms in under 30 seconds. If it passes, the commit is unlikely to break CI.

```bash
make validate
git add .
git diff --staged --stat   # review what is actually staged
git commit
```

The `git diff --staged --stat` step is worth making a habit; it is the last chance to catch an accidentally staged file before it enters the history.

### What not to commit

The `.gitignore` covers the main cases. As an extra reminder:

- `config/eff-large-wordlist.txt` is downloaded at setup time, not stored in the repo.
- Any real `ignition.json` is compiled output, regenerated from source.
- Build artefacts under `/var/lib/troskel/`.
- Scan logs under `/var/log/troskel/`.
- Any file containing a real password hash, key, or credential.

================================================================================

# Automate manual tests

`tests/manual-tests-scan.md` lists procedures that cannot run in CI
today: real-USB workflows, BadUSB simulation, freshness-gate
behaviour, HID injection scenarios. Each procedure is documented;
none is exercised by `make test`. A regression in any of them only
surfaces when an admin or operator runs the manual procedure by hand,
which they may not do.

The roadmap doc identifies which procedures are automatable in CI
(loop-device USB simulation, mocked freshness dates) versus which
need a hardware test rig (real HID injection, real BadUSB devices).

Roadmap doc: `docs/roadmap/automate-manual-tests.md`.

## Why it matters

The freshness-gate procedure is the one with the worst failure
shape: a silent regression here produces green verdicts against
stale signatures. The roadmap doc explicitly flags it as worth
pulling forward if the rest of this card slips. That carve-out
remains a fallback if 1.1.0 itself slips.

## Acceptance criteria

See the roadmap doc. Two days of work for the automatable
procedures; the rest stays manual with the existing documentation.

## Sequencing

1.1.0 cluster. No hard dependencies on other cards. The
freshness-gate piece can be carved out and landed earlier if
needed.

# Boot passphrase banner is an undocumented cross-script contract

`scripts/troskel-build.sh` parses the output of
`scripts/prepare-boot-usb.sh` to extract the per-build scanner
passphrase: an awk state machine keys on the `SCANNER PASSPHRASE` title
line and the `====` banner rules around the passphrase block. The
orchestrator side now documents this dependency (a CONTRACT NOTE on the
KEEP_OUT consumer, plus the mandatory emptiness check that fails loudly
if the format drifts). The producer side does not. `prepare-boot-usb.sh`
prints the banner with no comment noting that another script parses it,
so a well-meaning change to the banner wording or layout would silently
break extraction, caught only at runtime by the orchestrator's emptiness
guard.

## Motivation

QUALITY.md principle 3: any protocol spanning more than one script gets
a paragraph-length contract comment at both producer and consumer
sites, each naming the other. This one currently has the consumer half
only. The asymmetry is exactly the drift risk the principle exists to
prevent: the person most likely to change the banner is editing
`prepare-boot-usb.sh`, which is the file that carries no warning.

The emptiness check means a drift fails closed rather than silently
losing the passphrase, so this is low severity, but the contract
comment is near-zero cost and closes the gap the rule names.

## Current state

`prepare-boot-usb.sh` emits the banner block (title line containing
`SCANNER PASSPHRASE`, a `====` rule, the passphrase line, explanatory
text, a closing `====` rule) with no comment about downstream parsing.
`troskel-build.sh` carries the awk and a CONTRACT NOTE describing the
expected shape and the mandatory emptiness check.

## Target state

A paragraph-length contract comment at the banner-emitting site in
`prepare-boot-usb.sh` that:

- names `scripts/troskel-build.sh` as the consumer;
- states what is promised: the title line contains the literal
  `SCANNER PASSPHRASE`, the passphrase is the first non-empty line after
  the `====` rule that closes the header, and the block is closed by a
  `====` rule;
- warns that changing the banner layout requires updating the awk in the
  orchestrator, and that the orchestrator fails closed (aborts the run)
  rather than silently emitting an empty passphrase if the format
  drifts.

## Implementation outline

- Add the comment immediately above the banner-printing code in
  `prepare-boot-usb.sh`.
- Cross-check the wording against the orchestrator's CONTRACT NOTE so
  the two halves describe the same promise in the same terms.

## Side effects

None: comment only, no behaviour change.

## Failure modes to handle (per QUALITY.md)

Not applicable (documentation change). The runtime failure mode it
documents (banner drift) is already handled by the orchestrator's
emptiness check; this card does not change that path, only records it
at the producer.

## Estimated effort

Fifteen minutes.

## Sequencing

Not a blocker. Can ride along with any future edit to
`prepare-boot-usb.sh`, or with the manifest-propagation work
(`prepare-data-usb.sh` and friends) since that pass is already in those
scripts. Surfaced during the `troskel-build.sh` orchestration cleanup
when the boot stage was refactored to use run_step's KEEP_OUT.

================================================================================

# Capa as a third detection engine

The two current engines (ClamAV, LOKI-RS) are signature-based.
Capa is a behavioural-analysis engine from FLARE that identifies
malware capabilities by static analysis of compiled binaries.
Adding capa as a third engine widens detection coverage to
behaviours, not just signatures.

Roadmap doc: `docs/roadmap/capa-third-engine.md`.

## Why it matters

Capa catches malware that signature engines miss: novel families,
recompiled variants, packed samples whose unpacker is unrecognised.
At the cost of a longer scan and a richer verdict format.

## Acceptance criteria

See the roadmap doc. Two to three days plus open research
questions: rule-base management (capa rules update independently
of YARA), output integration into the verdict pipeline, runtime
budget (capa is slower than the signature engines).

## Sequencing

1.2.0 cluster. Wants `parallel-engines` to land first so capa is
a third independent VM rather than a third sequential step. Wants
`verdict-grammar` to land first so capa's behavioural categories
parse into the structured verdict cleanly.

Both are 1.2.0 cluster too, so capa is the natural last card in
that cluster. Realistically a 1.3.0 candidate.

## Open research

The roadmap doc lists open questions around licensing (capa is
Apache-2.0; the rule set has its own terms), runtime budget on
the scanning host, and the rule-base update workflow. None blocks
the technical work but each shapes it.

================================================================================

# Definition-version pre-login display

The scanning host's pre-login MOTD does not currently show the
signature versions of the loaded scanner. An operator logging in
cannot tell whether they are working with current detection rules
without running `show-status` first. For ad-hoc verification of
data-USB freshness, this is more friction than the value warrants.

Roadmap doc: `docs/roadmap/definition-version-display.md`.

## What this card delivers

A pre-login banner (via CoreOS Ignition or the host-scripts) that
shows the signature and YARA rules dates from the loaded data USB.
Read-only display; the actual freshness check stays in
`check-system-ready`.

## Acceptance criteria

See the roadmap doc. Half a day of work; isolated to host-scripts
and the Butane config.

## Sequencing

1.1.0 cluster. No dependencies on other backlog cards. Cheapest
operator-facing win in the 1.1.0 cluster; reasonable first card to
pick up when 1.0.0 ships.

FILE: .devtool/features/done/centralise-version-metadata-2026-06-16.md

# Centralise version metadata

The project version currently lives in seven string locations across
three files (README, the generator heredoc, and the committed
SBOM.json). The 0.9.0 to 1.0.0 bump audit found a stale `0.1.0`
reference that had survived multiple version bumps undetected: direct
evidence that hand-editing N copies does not converge, because nothing
forces the copies to agree.

## Motivation

Seven hand-maintained copies of a single fact means every bump is an
N-way edit with no check that the N agree. The failure mode is not
hypothetical: the audit already caught one copy two minor versions
stale. The risk a stale version carries here is not cosmetic. A
build-manifest or SBOM that reports the wrong version misattributes
which code and which signature set produced a given scan, which is a
provenance defect in a security-critical artefact.

## Target state

One canonical source for the version string. Every other location
derives from it at build time rather than carrying its own copy. After
the change, a version bump is a single edit, and any consumer that
needs the version reads or is generated from the canonical source.

## Acceptance criteria

- A single canonical version source exists (e.g. `config/versions.env`
  or an equivalent already in the tree; confirm the right home rather
  than introducing a new file if an existing one fits).
- The previously-enumerated seven locations no longer carry an
  independent literal. Each is either generated from, or reads from,
  the canonical source.
- A check that fails loudly on drift. Grepping the tree for a version
  literal that does not match the canonical source returns nothing, and
  this grep is wired into `make validate` (or the existing lint stage)
  so a reintroduced literal fails CI rather than surviving to a tag.
  This is the substantive guard: without it the change reduces the
  count from seven to one but does nothing to stop the count climbing
  back, which is the actual defect.
- The stale `0.1.0` survivor is confirmed eliminated, not merely
  outvoted: grep the tree for `0.1.0` and confirm zero hits outside
  legitimate changelog history.

## Failure mode to test

The regression test is the drift check itself: introduce a deliberate
mismatched version literal in a test fixture (or a throwaway branch)
and confirm `make validate` fails. A drift check that passes when a
mismatch is present is decorative. The test that proves the fix is the
one that would have caught the original `0.1.0` survivor at the commit
that introduced it.

## Implementation shapes

The superseded roadmap doc recorded two candidate implementation
shapes. That doc has been deleted and its content is not recoverable
from project state, so the two shapes are not reconstructed here rather
than guessed at. Re-derive the options at pickup from the actual tree:
the choice is broadly between build-time generation (canonical source,
all copies regenerated by the build) and read-at-runtime (consumers
read the canonical source directly). Decide based on which locations
are build artefacts versus committed files.

## Sequencing

Standalone; no dependencies on other cards. Cheap enough to land
opportunistically. Natural companion to the v1.0.0 release-gate card,
whose drift pass currently relies on a manual `0.1.0`/`0.9.1` grep as a
stopgap; this card is the durable replacement for that stopgap. Target:
land in the same commit as whatever first triggers the next version
bump after 0.9.1, plausibly the 1.0.0 tag itself.

================================================================================

# Defer 1.0.0 tag; ship 0.9.1 with bugfixes

The 1.0.0 plan defined the tag as a documentation and polish
milestone. Two silent-failure bugs in the pre-tag test cycle show
that the build pipeline does not yet enforce the security posture
even within the bounds the plan claimed. 1.0.0 should mean "the
foundations are sound", not "the documentation is polished".

Tag 0.9.1 now with the bug fixes already landed and in-flight.
Tag 1.0.0 after the quality-foundations work
(`quality-foundations-2026-06-16`) is done.

## Acceptance criteria

- README project-status block updated: still `0.9.x`, demonstrator,
  with a sentence noting the deferred 1.0.0 target.
- `SBOM.json` and the generator heredoc both at `0.9.1`.
- The road-to-1.0.0 plan doc (`docs/roadmap/road-to-1.0.0.md` if
  still extant; if deleted, re-create or update the relevant
  sequencing) updated to reflect the deferral: 1.0.0 blocked on
  the quality-foundations cards.
- `git tag -a v0.9.1` and push.

## Sequencing

Lands after both bug fixes are in (sidecar fix is done;
orchestrator fix is in-progress). 0.9.1 is the right tag because
the changes between 0.9.0 and now are bugfixes, not features.

## Notes

This card replaces the original steps 7 and 8 in the road-to-1.0.0
plan. Those steps assumed 1.0.0 would tag once drift cleanup and
metadata bump were done; the bugs uncovered since make that
unrealistic. The new path is: 0.9.1 now, 1.0.0 after foundations.

completedAt: "2026-06-17T12:41:36.131Z"
labels: ["quality", "docs"]
order: "a2"

# Extend system prompt with quality-bar rules

The current Troskel project instructions cover communication style,
formatting, and project conventions. They do not encode a quality
bar. Add a section that makes the rules from QUALITY.md operative
for AI-assisted work: any code Claude produces against this project
should follow them by default, not just when reminded.

## Acceptance criteria

The system prompt gains a "Quality bar" section covering:

- Success indicators must describe checks that could plausibly fail.
  Decorative checks are forbidden.
- `|| true` and similar error-swallowing patterns require a comment
  at the site of use naming why the failure is acceptable and what
  downstream code guards against the failure case.
- Cross-script protocols (file formats, env var contracts, exit code
  semantics) require a short contract comment at producer and
  consumer sites pointing at each other.
- Destructive operations (USB writes, partition table modification,
  any irrevocable action) require a verification step that re-reads
  from the destination, not from the source.
- Before writing the success path, name at least one failure mode
  the code must handle and how it will be tested.

The new section lives alongside the existing communication-style and
project-convention sections, not replacing them.

## Notes

This is the cheapest single change with the largest immediate
effect: it changes what gets written from now on, ahead of any code
rewrites. The QUALITY.md card produces the longer-form rationale;
this card produces the operative rules.

# Orchestrator hides write failures from inner scripts

`troskel-build.sh` runs `prepare-data-usb.sh` and `prepare-boot-usb.sh`
with captured output and reports a green tick based on exit code.
Inner scripts that fail silently (via `|| true` swallowing `umount`,
`wipefs`, or other errors) cause the orchestrator to report success
against USBs that were never written. Confirmed during the pre-1.0.0
test session: data USB reported as written, on inspection still
contained the original Fedora ISO content.

This is a silent safety failure: an operator cannot tell a successful
write from a swallowed-error no-op. For a security workflow where the
operator carries the USB to an air-gapped environment, this is the
worst possible failure shape.

Bug 2 (sidecar relative path) compounded this: even when the
orchestrator's verify step ran, it verified the source on the host
rather than the copy on the USB, so a never-written USB could also
pass verification. Bug 2 is fixed; this card is the remaining half.

## Acceptance criteria

- Inner script `umount`, `wipefs`, and other destructive-prep failures
  cause the inner script to exit non-zero.
- The orchestrator surfaces that exit code as a failed stage with the
  underlying error message visible, not buried behind `--debug`.
- `|| true` patterns swallowing errors on destructive-prep operations
  are removed or replaced with explicit-fail-with-message.
- A negative-case test (see `negative-case-test-orchestrator`) proves
  the orchestrator no longer reports success against a forced
  inner-script failure.

## Related

- Bug 2 (already fixed): `fix-sidecar-relative-path-2026-06-16`
- Roadmap doc: `docs/roadmap/build-orchestrator-progress.md` (the
  broader UX rewrite; this card is the narrower failure-propagation
  bug that must land before 1.0.0)

# Negative-case test: orchestrator propagates inner-script failures

The orchestrator silently reported success against an inner script
that failed with `|| true`-swallowed errors. A test that proves the
orchestrator surfaces failures would have caught the regression.

## Acceptance criteria

A test (in `tests/`, run as part of `make test`) that:

1. Creates a mock inner script that exits non-zero.
2. Invokes the orchestrator's stage runner against the mock.
3. Asserts the orchestrator exits non-zero.
4. Asserts the orchestrator surfaces the mock's error message to
   stdout/stderr, not buried behind `--debug`.

A second test variant: the mock inner script swallows its own
exit code with `exit 0` after a destructive failure. The
orchestrator must detect this by checking observable side effects
(e.g. did the artefact get written) and fail loudly.

The second variant is harder and may need design work; if so, the
first variant lands now and the second becomes its own card. Both
must land before 1.0.0.

## Notes

Depends on the orchestrator failure-propagation fix
(`fix-orchestrator-failure-propagation-2026-06-16`) landing first.
This card is the regression alarm; the fix card is the fix.

# Negative-case test: sidecar verify catches USB corruption

The sidecar bug just fixed went undetected because the test suite
exercised only the happy path. A test that proves the verifier
actually catches a corrupt USB would have caught the bug at
introduction.

## Acceptance criteria

A test (in `tests/`, run as part of `make test`) that:

1. Writes a USB image to a loop device (no physical USB required).
2. Deliberately corrupts the image after the write (flip a byte
   somewhere in the middle of the file).
3. Runs the verification logic.
4. Asserts that verification fails.

The test must fail under the pre-fix code (absolute-path sidecar)
and pass under the post-fix code (relative-path sidecar). This is
the proof the fix is correct and the alarm if it regresses.

## Notes

Use a loop device, not a real USB, so the test is hermetic and
CI-runnable. The test should not depend on hardware.

This card is part of the broader quality-foundations work
(`quality-foundations-2026-06-16`). It is the first concrete test
that exercises a failure mode rather than a success path.
